# Vishnu Sahasranama through an Adi Shankaracharya lens

This version keeps the thousand names devotional, but reads them in a Shankara-shaped way: Vishnu as Ishvara, the inner Self of all beings, and the one Brahman toward which names, forms, and worship finally point.

## Reading note

This is an Advaita-oriented companion, not a substitute for the full Sanskrit bhashya. The meanings stay compact, while the interpretive note leans toward Shankara's stress on sarvatmakatva, witness-consciousness, upasana, and the movement from saguna contemplation toward brahma-jnana.

## How to use this file

- This file is intentionally shaped by an Advaita orientation associated with Adi Shankaracharya's Vishnu Sahasranama bhashya.
- The `Meaning` field remains compact, while `Shankara lens` emphasizes the movement from form and devotion toward the recognition of Vishnu as the inner Self and Brahman.
- The Puranic stories are kept as aids to meditation and bhakti, not as limiting the name to one historical episode alone.

## Names 1-100

### 1. viśvam (विश्वम्)
- Meaning: Who is the universe himself.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: When mother Yashoda asked Krishna to open his mouth, she saw worlds within him; this name fits the Lord whose apparent smallness can suddenly reveal totality.

### 2. viṣṇuḥ (विष्णुः)
- Meaning: He who pervades everywhere.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: In the Gita's Vishvarupa revelation, Arjuna beholds all beings and all time in Krishna; this name shines where Vishnu appears as the cosmic whole.

### 3. vaṣaṭkāraḥ (वषट्कारः)
- Meaning: On whose account oblations are offered in fire.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that ritual is fulfilled when it matures into inner offering and knowledge of the divine center.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by treating daily action as worship that should purify the mind, not merely accumulate results.
- Story: In the churning of the ocean, gods and asuras labor for nectar, but the whole enterprise reaches order only through Vishnu's oversight; this name shows the Lord as the hidden receiver of sacrifice.

### 4. bhūta-bhavya-bhavat-prabhuḥ (भूतभव्यभवत्प्रभुः)
- Meaning: The lord of past, present and future.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: During pralaya, Markandeya sees the infant Narayana on the banyan leaf holding the universe in serene play; that vision matches this boundless epithet.

### 5. bhūtakṛt (भूतकृत्)
- Meaning: Creator of all creatures.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: From the lotus springing out of Vishnu's navel, Brahma begins creation; this name recalls the Lord as the hidden ground of all worlds.

### 6. bhūtabhṛt (भूतभृत्)
- Meaning: The sustainer of all creatures.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: Vamana's three strides cover earth, heaven, and the regions between; this name becomes visible in that act of all-pervasion.

### 7. bhāvaḥ (भावः)
- Meaning: He who is in the form of pure emotions.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: Prahlada insists that Hari is present everywhere, even in a pillar; this name is affirmed by that fearless vision of omnipresence.

### 8. bhūtātmā (भूतात्मा)
- Meaning: The soul of all beings.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: In the Bhagavata, Krishna expands himself for every gopa and calf during Brahma's bewilderment; this name suits the Lord who is one yet all.

### 9. bhūtabhāvanaḥ (भूतभावनः)
- Meaning: He who nurtures all beings.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Narayana resting on the cosmic ocean before manifest creation embodies this name as quiet totality before differentiation.

### 10. pūtātmā (पूतात्मा)
- Meaning: He who has a pure self.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: When Akrura enters the Yamuna and beholds Vishnu with Ananta, he sees the transcendent form within the ordinary world; that is this name in narrative form.

### 11. paramātmā (परमात्मा)
- Meaning: The supreme soul.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Dhruva's austerity ends in a vision of the Lord whose presence fills inner and outer space alike; this name belongs to that overwhelming encounter.

### 12. muktānāṁ parama-gatiḥ (मुक्तानां परमागतिः)
- Meaning: The ultimate goal of all liberated souls.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that the Lord praised here is also the final truth in whose knowledge bondage ends.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using sorrow itself as a doorway to discern the difference between passing states and the real.
- Story: Dhruva seeks a kingdom but receives direct vision and a transformed heart; this name matches the Lord who turns ambition toward liberation.

### 13. avyayaḥ (अव्ययः)
- Meaning: He who is above destruction or change.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: Garuda carries the Lord across the worlds, yet no place contains him; the story reinforces this name's claim that Vishnu transcends location.

### 14. puruṣaḥ (पुरुषः)
- Meaning: The supreme spirit.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: At the close of each kalpa, the worlds fold back into Narayana; this name points to that cosmic re-absorption.

### 15. sākṣī (साक्षी)
- Meaning: The witness.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a name especially useful for shifting from conceptual study into stillness.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by letting silence become a way of listening to the presence already nearer than thought.
- Story: Dhruva's tapas steadies the whole cosmos and culminates in Vishnu's vision; this name fits the Lord discovered through unwavering concentration.

### 16. kṣetrajñaḥ (क्षेत्रज्ञः)
- Meaning: The knower of the field.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a contemplative bridge from sacred word to direct recognition of the self-luminous reality.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by letting the name turn curiosity into discrimination and discrimination into stillness.
- Story: Krishna instructs Arjuna on the battlefield, turning despair into discernment; this name belongs to the Lord who teaches inside crisis.

### 17. akṣaraḥ (अक्षरः)
- Meaning: He who is immutable.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: When mother Yashoda asked Krishna to open his mouth, she saw worlds within him; this name fits the Lord whose apparent smallness can suddenly reveal totality.

### 18. yogaḥ (योगः)
- Meaning: He who is realized through yoga.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a direct support for inwardness, witness-awareness, and mind-gathering contemplation.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by bringing the mind back to witnessing whenever it becomes overrun by reaction.
- Story: Narada's instruction turns grief and restlessness into focused devotion; this epithet suits the inner guidance of spiritual discipline.

### 19. yogavidāṁ netā (योगविदां नेता)
- Meaning: The leader of those who know yoga.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a direct support for inwardness, witness-awareness, and mind-gathering contemplation.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by bringing the mind back to witnessing whenever it becomes overrun by reaction.
- Story: The sages who meditate upon Narayana in Badarika embody this name as contemplative steadiness directed toward the supreme person.

### 20. pradhāna-puruṣeśvaraḥ (प्रधानपुरुषेश्वरः)
- Meaning: The lord of matter and spirit.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: In the Gita's Vishvarupa revelation, Arjuna beholds all beings and all time in Krishna; this name shines where Vishnu appears as the cosmic whole.

### 21. nārasiṁha-vapuḥ (नारसिंहवपुः)
- Meaning: He whose form is man-lion.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that avatara names are not metaphysical limitations of Brahman but compassionate manifestations for seekers.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by allowing the story to hold the heart steady until deeper understanding becomes possible.
- Story: Prahlada's unwavering faith draws Narasimha from the pillar, making this name the triumph of omnipresent grace over engineered cruelty.

### 22. śrīmān (श्रीमान्)
- Meaning: He who always has Sri with him.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that sacred radiance is not opposed to truth but can refine the mind toward it.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by seeing beauty as a support for recollection rather than as a distraction to be resented.
- Story: At the emergence of Lakshmi from the milk ocean, she chooses Vishnu as her eternal abode; this name naturally carries the glow of that union.

### 23. keśavaḥ (केशवः)
- Meaning: He who has beautiful hair.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a reminder that cosmic texture is not independent substance but appearance upheld in consciousness.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by observing change in the world while remembering the changeless that makes change knowable.
- Story: Varaha lifting the earth from cosmic waters makes elemental imagery literal; this name suits Vishnu as guardian of the world-body.

### 24. puruṣottamaḥ (पुरुषोत्तमः)
- Meaning: The supreme puruṣa.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.

### 25. sarvaḥ (सर्वः)

### 26. śarvaḥ (शर्वः)
- Meaning: The auspicious one.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a name in which Sri becomes a contemplative symbol of harmony, grace, and all-sided completeness.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by redefining prosperity as inward clarity plus wise stewardship of what has been given.
- Story: In Tirumala lore, Srinivasa receives and protects the wealth of devotion offered by countless pilgrims; such narratives illuminate auspicious names.

### 27. śivaḥ (शिवः)
- Meaning: The ever pure one.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Vamana's three strides cover earth, heaven, and the regions between; this name becomes visible in that act of all-pervasion.

### 28. sthāṇuḥ (स्थाणुः)
- Meaning: The pillar, the immovable truth.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a revelation of Vishnu as witness-consciousness and as the light by which scripture and experience become intelligible.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by joining study, self-inquiry, and devotion instead of separating them into different compartments.
- Story: As Hayagriva, Vishnu restores the Vedas after they are stolen; the story suits names tied to knowledge and sacred speech.

### 29. bhūtādiḥ (भूतादिः)

- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.

### 30. nidhir-avyayaḥ (निधिरव्ययः)
- Meaning: The imperishable treasure.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that the Lord praised here is also the final truth in whose knowledge bondage ends.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using sorrow itself as a doorway to discern the difference between passing states and the real.
- Story: Gajendra's rescue is not merely escape from a crocodile but deliverance from bondage and forgetfulness; this epithet fits that deeper release.

### 31. sambhavaḥ (सम्भवः)

### 36. īśvaraḥ (ईश्वरः)
- Meaning: The ruler.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a name that places time, sequence, and change inside the governance of timeless reality.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by accepting timing, patience, and ripening as part of a sacred process rather than an insult to your plans.
- Story: The cyclic creation and dissolution described in the Puranas show kalpas moving within Narayana's will; this name belongs to the Lord behind vast rhythms.

### 44. vidhātā (विधाता)
- Meaning: The law-giver.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an aid to seeing that calendar, causation, and destiny belong to vyavahara, not to the absolute as such.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by remembering that what changes in time is not the deepest self.
- Story: Krishna delays open confrontation with Kamsa until the right moment, showing time used as instrument rather than obstacle.

### 45. dhātur-uttamaḥ (धातुरुत्तमः)

### 53. sthaviṣṭhaḥ (स्थविष्ठः)
- Meaning: The most massive.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an Upasana-friendly name that pulls outward worship back toward the one inner receiver of all sacred action.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by remembering that the deepest oblation is ego-centeredness itself.
- Story: As Yajna in primordial times, Vishnu upholds cosmic order through sacrificial harmony; the name fits the deity who is both rite and fruit.

### 54. sthaviro dhruvaḥ (स्थविरो ध्रुवः)

- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.

- Story: In the Gita's Vishvarupa revelation, Arjuna beholds all beings and all time in Krishna; this name shines where Vishnu appears as the cosmic whole.

### 55. agrāhyaḥ (अग्राह्यः)

- Story: Narasimha bursts forth to save Prahlada and break tyrannical pride; this name fits the Lord whose protection arrives exactly where hope seems blocked.

- Story: When Akrura enters the Yamuna and beholds Vishnu with Ananta, he sees the transcendent form within the ordinary world; that is this name in narrative form.

### 111. puṇḍarīkākṣaḥ (पुण्डरीकाक्षः)
- Meaning: Lotus-eyed one.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that sacred radiance is not opposed to truth but can refine the mind toward it.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by seeing beauty as a support for recollection rather than as a distraction to be resented.
- Story: The Lord seated with Sri on his chest symbolizes a kingship inseparable from compassion and harmony; this name points to that inseparable splendor.

### 112. vṛṣakarmā (वृषकर्मा)
- Meaning: Performer of righteous acts.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: Dhruva's austerity ends in a vision of the Lord whose presence fills inner and outer space alike; this name belongs to that overwhelming encounter.

### 113. vṛṣākṛtiḥ (वृषाकृतिः)

### 166. vīrahā (वीरहा)
- Meaning: Slayer of the mighty.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: In the Gita's Vishvarupa revelation, Arjuna beholds all beings and all time in Krishna; this name shines where Vishnu appears as the cosmic whole.

### 167. mādhavaḥ (माधवः)
- Meaning: Lord of sweet wisdom and springlike grace.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a name that links devotion to viveka, because the Lord is both the revealer of truth and the ground of knowing.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by asking not only what is happening, but who is the knower in whose light the happening is known.
- Story: The child Dhruva receives mantra and then direct vision, showing that true knowledge matures from remembrance into realization.

### 168. madhuḥ (मधुः)
- Meaning: Sweetness itself.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: During pralaya, Markandeya sees the infant Narayana on the banyan leaf holding the universe in serene play; that vision matches this boundless epithet.

### 169. atīndriyaḥ (अतीन्द्रियः)
- Meaning: Beyond the senses.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: From the lotus springing out of Vishnu's navel, Brahma begins creation; this name recalls the Lord as the hidden ground of all worlds.

### 170. mahāmāyaḥ (महामायः)
- Meaning: Master of wondrous power.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: Vamana's three strides cover earth, heaven, and the regions between; this name becomes visible in that act of all-pervasion.

### 171. mahotsāhaḥ (महोत्साहः)
- Meaning: Of great enthusiasm.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Prahlada insists that Hari is present everywhere, even in a pillar; this name is affirmed by that fearless vision of omnipresence.

### 172. mahābalaḥ (महाबलः)
- Meaning: Of immense strength.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: In the Bhagavata, Krishna expands himself for every gopa and calf during Brahma's bewilderment; this name suits the Lord who is one yet all.

### 173. mahābuddhiḥ (महाबुद्धिः)
- Meaning: Of vast intelligence.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Narayana resting on the cosmic ocean before manifest creation embodies this name as quiet totality before differentiation.

### 174. mahāvīryaḥ (महावीर्यः)
- Meaning: Of supreme heroism.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: When Akrura enters the Yamuna and beholds Vishnu with Ananta, he sees the transcendent form within the ordinary world; that is this name in narrative form.

### 175. mahāśaktiḥ (महाशक्तिः)
- Meaning: Of immense power.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: Dhruva's austerity ends in a vision of the Lord whose presence fills inner and outer space alike; this name belongs to that overwhelming encounter.

### 176. mahādyutiḥ (महाद्युतिः)
- Meaning: Of great radiance.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: Garuda carries the Lord across the worlds, yet no place contains him; the story reinforces this name's claim that Vishnu transcends location.

### 177. anirdeśya-vapuḥ (अनिर्देश्यवपुः)
- Meaning: Of indescribable form.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: At the close of each kalpa, the worlds fold back into Narayana; this name points to that cosmic re-absorption.

### 178. śrīmān (श्रीमान्)
- Meaning: Ever endowed with Sri.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a name in which Sri becomes a contemplative symbol of harmony, grace, and all-sided completeness.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by redefining prosperity as inward clarity plus wise stewardship of what has been given.
- Story: Tulasi's devotion becomes eternally joined to Vishnu's worship, showing that auspiciousness includes purity of offering and love.

### 179. ameyātmā (अमेयात्मा)
- Meaning: Of immeasurable essence.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: When mother Yashoda asked Krishna to open his mouth, she saw worlds within him; this name fits the Lord whose apparent smallness can suddenly reveal totality.

### 180. mahādridhṛk (महाद्रिधृक्)
- Meaning: Bearer of the great mountain.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a way of reading the elements as nama-rupa dependent on one underlying reality.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by turning sky, light, wind, and water into meditation prompts instead of background scenery.
- Story: Krishna dances upon Kaliya in the Yamuna, purifying poisoned waters; this name aligns with divine mastery within nature.

### 181. maheṣvāsaḥ (महेष्वासः)
- Meaning: Wielder of the great bow.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a symbolic praise of the Lord's power to cut avidya, protect dharma, and remove inner obstruction.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by letting discrimination cut confusion before it grows into habit.
- Story: Krishna's discus severs Shishupala's arrogance at the Rajasuya after long patience, making this name one of measured justice.

### 182. mahībhartā (महीभर्ता)

### 183. śrīnivāsaḥ (श्रीनिवासः)

- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by seeing beauty as a support for recollection rather than as a distraction to be resented.
- Story: The Samudra Manthana produces many treasures, yet Lakshmi's choosing of Vishnu reveals where true prosperity ultimately rests.

### 184. satāṁ gatiḥ (सतां गतिः)

- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that the Lord praised here is also the final truth in whose knowledge bondage ends.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by using sorrow itself as a doorway to discern the difference between passing states and the real.
- Story: Ajamila's last-minute remembrance opens a path beyond the mechanics of punishment; this name points to grace beyond despair.

### 208. surārihā (सुरारिहा)

- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by trusting order without becoming passive, and doing your dharma while leaving total control to the Lord.
- Story: Gajendra's appeal from the lake brings Vishnu immediately on Garuda; this epithet lives in that swift rescue of the desperate.

### 209. guruḥ (गुरुः)

- Story: Narada repeatedly carries divine insight into confused situations, and his guidance ultimately points back to Vishnu; this name aligns with such illuminating grace.

- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: During pralaya, Markandeya sees the infant Narayana on the banyan leaf holding the universe in serene play; that vision matches this boundless epithet.

### 223. samīraṇaḥ (समीरणः)
- Meaning: The life-giving wind.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a contemplative hint that what seems manifold in nature rests in one unfragmented truth.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by allowing elemental experience to point beyond itself toward the one reality it depends on.
- Story: The serpent Ananta becomes Vishnu's couch, revealing even immense natural force as restful service in the divine presence.

### 224. sahasramūrdhā (सहस्रमूर्धा)
- Meaning: Thousand-headed.

- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: From the lotus springing out of Vishnu's navel, Brahma begins creation; this name recalls the Lord as the hidden ground of all worlds.

### 225. viśvātmā (विश्वात्मा)
- Meaning: Soul of the universe.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Vamana's three strides cover earth, heaven, and the regions between; this name becomes visible in that act of all-pervasion.

### 228. āvartanaḥ (आवर्तनः)

- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using the name when restless about results; it helps distinguish eternal value from temporary sequence.
- Story: Vamana's measured three steps transform cosmic space into sacred order; this epithet reflects the Lord as measurer and ordainer.

### 229. nivṛttātmā (निवृत्तात्मा)
- Meaning: Withdrawn from worldly involvement.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: Narayana resting on the cosmic ocean before manifest creation embodies this name as quiet totality before differentiation.

### 230. saṁvṛtaḥ (संवृतः)

### 231. sampramardanaḥ (सम्प्रमर्दनः)

- Story: At the close of each kalpa, the worlds fold back into Narayana; this name points to that cosmic re-absorption.

### 278. ṛddhaḥ (ऋद्धः)
- Meaning: Ever flourishing.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: When mother Yashoda asked Krishna to open his mouth, she saw worlds within him; this name fits the Lord whose apparent smallness can suddenly reveal totality.

### 279. spaṣṭākṣaraḥ (स्पष्टाक्षरः)
- Meaning: Clearly expressed, the manifest syllable.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: In the Gita's Vishvarupa revelation, Arjuna beholds all beings and all time in Krishna; this name shines where Vishnu appears as the cosmic whole.

### 280. mantraḥ (मन्त्रः)
- Meaning: The sacred mantra.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a revelation of Vishnu as witness-consciousness and as the light by which scripture and experience become intelligible.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by joining study, self-inquiry, and devotion instead of separating them into different compartments.
- Story: As Hayagriva, Vishnu restores the Vedas after they are stolen; the story suits names tied to knowledge and sacred speech.

### 281. candrāṁśuḥ (चन्द्रांशुः)
- Meaning: Moon-rayed.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a way of reading the elements as nama-rupa dependent on one underlying reality.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by turning sky, light, wind, and water into meditation prompts instead of background scenery.
- Story: Varaha lifting the earth from cosmic waters makes elemental imagery literal; this name suits Vishnu as guardian of the world-body.

### 282. bhāskaradyutiḥ (भास्करद्युतिः)
- Meaning: Radiant like the sun.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that cosmic texture is not independent substance but appearance upheld in consciousness.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by observing change in the world while remembering the changeless that makes change knowable.
- Story: Kurma supports Mount Mandara during the churning, turning mountain and ocean alike into instruments of divine purpose.

### 283. amṛtāṁśūdbhavaḥ (अमृतांशूद्भवः)
- Meaning: Source of the moon.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that cosmic texture is not independent substance but appearance upheld in consciousness.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by observing change in the world while remembering the changeless that makes change knowable.
- Story: Matsya guides the ark through the deluge, showing the Lord present in waters both destructive and protective.

### 284. bhānuḥ (भानुः)
- Meaning: The shining one.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: During pralaya, Markandeya sees the infant Narayana on the banyan leaf holding the universe in serene play; that vision matches this boundless epithet.

### 285. śaśabinduḥ (शशबिन्दुः)
- Meaning: Moon-marked or moon-like.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a contemplative hint that what seems manifold in nature rests in one unfragmented truth.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by allowing elemental experience to point beyond itself toward the one reality it depends on.
- Story: Krishna dances upon Kaliya in the Yamuna, purifying poisoned waters; this name aligns with divine mastery within nature.

### 286. sureśvaraḥ (सुरेश्वरः)
- Meaning: Lord of the devas.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: From the lotus springing out of Vishnu's navel, Brahma begins creation; this name recalls the Lord as the hidden ground of all worlds.

### 287. auṣadham (औषधम्)

### 288. jagataḥ setuḥ (जगतः सेतुः)

- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Prahlada insists that Hari is present everywhere, even in a pillar; this name is affirmed by that fearless vision of omnipresence.

### 289. satyadharma-parākramaḥ (सत्यधर्मपराक्रमः)
- Meaning: Whose valor protects truth and dharma.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as an upasana-rich name: form is honored as a valid doorway through which the mind approaches the formless truth.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by meditating on the form lovingly while remembering that the form is a doorway, not a boundary.
- Story: The reunion with Bharata displays a form of sovereignty anchored in restraint rather than possession.

### 290. bhūta-bhavya-bhavannāthaḥ (भूतभव्यभवन्नाथः)

- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by trusting order without becoming passive, and doing your dharma while leaving total control to the Lord.
- Story: Krishna breaks Kamsa's reign after years of hidden preparation; this name reflects a protection that can be patient before it becomes dramatic.

### 307. anantajit (अनन्तजित्)

### 333. bṛhadbhānuḥ (बृहद्भानुः)
- Meaning: Of vast radiance.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: From the lotus springing out of Vishnu's navel, Brahma begins creation; this name recalls the Lord as the hidden ground of all worlds.

### 334. ādidevaḥ (आदिदेवः)
- Meaning: The primordial deity.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Vamana's three strides cover earth, heaven, and the regions between; this name becomes visible in that act of all-pervasion.

### 335. purandaraḥ (पुरन्दरः)
- Meaning: Destroyer of hostile cities.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a saguna-Ishvara name through which grace, order, and dharmic correction become meditatively approachable.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by trusting order without becoming passive, and doing your dharma while leaving total control to the Lord.
- Story: The Sudarshana protects Ambarisha from Durvasa's fury, proving this name through preservation of the humble devotee.

### 336. aśokaḥ (अशोकः)
- Meaning: Free from sorrow.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: Prahlada insists that Hari is present everywhere, even in a pillar; this name is affirmed by that fearless vision of omnipresence.

### 337. tāraṇaḥ (तारणः)
- Meaning: He who carries across.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: In the Bhagavata, Krishna expands himself for every gopa and calf during Brahma's bewilderment; this name suits the Lord who is one yet all.

### 338. tāraḥ (तारः)
- Meaning: The savior, the deliverer.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an affirmation that the ruling Lord is not inert principle but conscious governance present in the moral order.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by asking where divine protection in your life should become ethical steadiness rather than mere emotional comfort.
- Story: Krishna safeguards Parikshit in the womb from Ashvatthama's weapon; the name fits that unseen guardianship of future dharma.

### 339. śūraḥ (शूरः)
- Meaning: The heroic one.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: Narayana resting on the cosmic ocean before manifest creation embodies this name as quiet totality before differentiation.

### 340. śauriḥ (शौरिः)

### 341. janeśvaraḥ (जनेश्वरः)

### 342. anukūlaḥ (अनुकूलः)

### 343. śatāvartaḥ (शतावर्तः)

### 344. padmī (पद्मी)

### 345. padmanibhekṣaṇaḥ (पद्मनिभेक्षणः)

- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Vamana's three strides cover earth, heaven, and the regions between; this name becomes visible in that act of all-pervasion.

### 389. pararddhiḥ (परर्द्धिः)
- Meaning: Of supreme prosperity.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Prahlada insists that Hari is present everywhere, even in a pillar; this name is affirmed by that fearless vision of omnipresence.

### 390. paramaspaṣṭaḥ (परमस्पष्टः)
- Meaning: Supremely clear and self-evident.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: In the Bhagavata, Krishna expands himself for every gopa and calf during Brahma's bewilderment; this name suits the Lord who is one yet all.

### 391. tuṣṭaḥ (तुष्टः)
- Meaning: Content and satisfied.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: Narayana resting on the cosmic ocean before manifest creation embodies this name as quiet totality before differentiation.

### 392. puṣṭaḥ (पुष्टः)
- Meaning: Nourished and nourishing.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: When Akrura enters the Yamuna and beholds Vishnu with Ananta, he sees the transcendent form within the ordinary world; that is this name in narrative form.

### 393. śubhekṣaṇaḥ (शुभेक्षणः)
- Meaning: Of auspicious glance.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a name in which Sri becomes a contemplative symbol of harmony, grace, and all-sided completeness.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by redefining prosperity as inward clarity plus wise stewardship of what has been given.
- Story: In the story of Andal's longing for Ranganatha, divine beauty becomes an object of total surrender; this name resonates with that magnetic grace.

### 394. rāmaḥ (रामः)
- Meaning: He who delights, or Rama himself.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a form-centered praise that steadies devotion while quietly training the mind toward the limitless reality behind form.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by using personal devotion as the emotional purification that prepares the mind for knowledge.
- Story: The bridge to Lanka shows leadership that gathers many beings into one dharmic purpose.

### 395. virāmaḥ (विरामः)
- Meaning: The resting place, the pause.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a form-centered praise that steadies devotion while quietly training the mind toward the limitless reality behind form.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by using personal devotion as the emotional purification that prepares the mind for knowledge.
- Story: Rama's protection of the sages in Dandaka reveals divine kingship expressed through service.

### 396. virajaḥ (विरजः)
- Meaning: Free from passion and stain.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Dhruva's austerity ends in a vision of the Lord whose presence fills inner and outer space alike; this name belongs to that overwhelming encounter.

### 397. mārgaḥ (मार्गः)
- Meaning: The path.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Garuda carries the Lord across the worlds, yet no place contains him; the story reinforces this name's claim that Vishnu transcends location.

### 398. neyaḥ (नेयः)
- Meaning: He who guides.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: At the close of each kalpa, the worlds fold back into Narayana; this name points to that cosmic re-absorption.

### 399. nayaḥ (नयः)
- Meaning: The leader, right conduct.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: When mother Yashoda asked Krishna to open his mouth, she saw worlds within him; this name fits the Lord whose apparent smallness can suddenly reveal totality.

### 400. anayaḥ (अनयः)
- Meaning: Beyond all finite methods.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: In the Gita's Vishvarupa revelation, Arjuna beholds all beings and all time in Krishna; this name shines where Vishnu appears as the cosmic whole.

## Names 401-500

### 401. vīraḥ (वीरः)
- Meaning: The heroic one.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: During pralaya, Markandeya sees the infant Narayana on the banyan leaf holding the universe in serene play; that vision matches this boundless epithet.

### 402. śaktimatāṁ śreṣṭhaḥ (शक्तिमतां श्रेष्ठः)
- Meaning: Best among the powerful.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: From the lotus springing out of Vishnu's navel, Brahma begins creation; this name recalls the Lord as the hidden ground of all worlds.

### 403. dharmaḥ (धर्मः)

- Story: Kapila teaches Devahuti the way of liberation and right seeing; this name resonates with Vishnu as clarifying intelligence.

- Story: Narasimha bursts forth to save Prahlada and break tyrannical pride; this name fits the Lord whose protection arrives exactly where hope seems blocked.

### 413. vyāptaḥ (व्याप्तः)

### 414. vāyuḥ (वायुः)
- Meaning: The life-breathing wind.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a way of reading the elements as nama-rupa dependent on one underlying reality.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by turning sky, light, wind, and water into meditation prompts instead of background scenery.
- Story: In the forest episodes of the Ramayana, trees, rivers, and mountains become witnesses to Rama's dharma; this name turns the landscape into theology.

### 415. adhokṣajaḥ (अधोक्षजः)

### 416. ṛtuḥ (ऋतुः)
- Meaning: Sacred season, cosmic rhythm.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a name that places time, sequence, and change inside the governance of timeless reality.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by accepting timing, patience, and ripening as part of a sacred process rather than an insult to your plans.
- Story: The return of the monsoon after Govardhana's lesson reminds Indra that power too has a rightful rhythm under higher law.

### 417. sudarśanaḥ (सुदर्शनः)
- Meaning: Of beautiful vision; the discus-bearing Lord.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a vivid devotional image in which divine instruments stand for precise correction in the field of ignorance.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by asking the Lord to remove inner enemies with the same decisiveness shown in sacred iconography.
- Story: In the war against Narakasura, Vishnu's weapons restore balance by removing predatory power; this name fits that corrective force.

### 418. kālaḥ (कालः)
- Meaning: Time itself.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that the Lord presides over temporal process while remaining untouched by its mutations.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by using the name when restless about results; it helps distinguish eternal value from temporary sequence.
- Story: Krishna's promise that dharma is restored age after age frames this name in the long continuity of divine intervention.

### 419. parameṣṭhī (परमेष्ठी)
- Meaning: Seated in the highest place.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a reminder that cosmic texture is not independent substance but appearance upheld in consciousness.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by observing change in the world while remembering the changeless that makes change knowable.
- Story: Varaha lifting the earth from cosmic waters makes elemental imagery literal; this name suits Vishnu as guardian of the world-body.

### 420. parigrahaḥ (परिग्रहः)

### 422. saṁvatsaraḥ (संवत्सरः)
- Meaning: The year, cyclical time.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an aid to seeing that calendar, causation, and destiny belong to vyavahara, not to the absolute as such.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by remembering that what changes in time is not the deepest self.
- Story: The cyclic creation and dissolution described in the Puranas show kalpas moving within Narayana's will; this name belongs to the Lord behind vast rhythms.

### 423. dakṣaḥ (दक्षः)

### 425. viśvadakṣiṇaḥ (विश्वदक्षिणः)

- Story: When Krishna teaches that offerings made with devotion are accepted even if simple, this epithet becomes inward and universal.

- Story: Prahlada insists that Hari is present everywhere, even in a pillar; this name is affirmed by that fearless vision of omnipresence.

### 445. yajñaḥ (यज्ञः)
- Meaning: Sacrifice itself.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that ritual is fulfilled when it matures into inner offering and knowledge of the divine center.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by treating daily action as worship that should purify the mind, not merely accumulate results.
- Story: In Ambarisha's observance of Ekadashi and Dvadashi, discipline itself becomes worship; this name suits Vishnu as the fulfiller of vowed offering.

### 446. ijyaḥ (इज्यः)

### 447. mahejyaḥ (महेज्यः)

### 450. satāṁ gatiḥ (सतां गतिः)

- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by asking what you still take to be absolutely necessary even though it cannot survive change.
- Story: Bharata's later detachment after the deer episode illustrates how the Lord patiently leads the soul beyond subtle attachments; this name resonates there.

### 451. sarvadarśī (सर्वदर्शी)

- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.

- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: At the close of each kalpa, the worlds fold back into Narayana; this name points to that cosmic re-absorption.

## Names 501-600

### 501. kapīndraḥ (कपीन्द्रः)
- Meaning: Lord among beings of strength; also monkey-lord ally.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: When mother Yashoda asked Krishna to open his mouth, she saw worlds within him; this name fits the Lord whose apparent smallness can suddenly reveal totality.

### 502. bhūridakṣiṇaḥ (भूरिदक्षिणः)
- Meaning: Bountiful giver.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: In the Gita's Vishvarupa revelation, Arjuna beholds all beings and all time in Krishna; this name shines where Vishnu appears as the cosmic whole.

### 503. somapaḥ (सोमपः)
- Meaning: Drinker of soma.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an Upasana-friendly name that pulls outward worship back toward the one inner receiver of all sacred action.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by remembering that the deepest oblation is ego-centeredness itself.
- Story: In the churning of the ocean, gods and asuras labor for nectar, but the whole enterprise reaches order only through Vishnu's oversight; this name shows the Lord as the hidden receiver of sacrifice.

### 504. amṛtapaḥ (अमृतपः)
- Meaning: Drinker of immortality.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: During pralaya, Markandeya sees the infant Narayana on the banyan leaf holding the universe in serene play; that vision matches this boundless epithet.

### 505. somaḥ (सोमः)
- Meaning: The moonlike, soothing one.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a way of seeing sacrifice, offerer, offering, and fruit as resting in one Brahman through Ishvara.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by offering speech, labor, food, and restraint inwardly to the Lord rather than performing them with vanity.
- Story: As Yajna in primordial times, Vishnu upholds cosmic order through sacrificial harmony; the name fits the deity who is both rite and fruit.

### 506. purujit (पुरुजित्)
- Meaning: Conqueror of many.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a saguna-Ishvara name through which grace, order, and dharmic correction become meditatively approachable.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by trusting order without becoming passive, and doing your dharma while leaving total control to the Lord.
- Story: Rama defends the sages of the forest and keeps his father's word despite hardship; this name honors steadfast protective dharma.

### 507. puruṣattamaḥ (पुरुषत्तमः)
- Meaning: Best of persons.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: From the lotus springing out of Vishnu's navel, Brahma begins creation; this name recalls the Lord as the hidden ground of all worlds.

### 508. vinayaḥ (विनयः)
- Meaning: Discipline and humility.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: Vamana's three strides cover earth, heaven, and the regions between; this name becomes visible in that act of all-pervasion.

### 509. jayaḥ (जयः)
- Meaning: Victory.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an affirmation that the ruling Lord is not inert principle but conscious governance present in the moral order.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by asking where divine protection in your life should become ethical steadiness rather than mere emotional comfort.
- Story: Vishnu destroys Madhu and Kaitabha when cosmic order is threatened; the story shows protection at the scale of creation itself.

### 510. satyasaṅdhaḥ (सत्यसन्धः)
- Meaning: True to his promise.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: Prahlada insists that Hari is present everywhere, even in a pillar; this name is affirmed by that fearless vision of omnipresence.

### 511. dāśārhaḥ (दाशार्हः)
- Meaning: Of the Yadava line.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: In the Bhagavata, Krishna expands himself for every gopa and calf during Brahma's bewilderment; this name suits the Lord who is one yet all.

### 512. sātvataṁ patiḥ (सात्वतां पतिः)
- Meaning: Lord of the Satvatas.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: Narayana resting on the cosmic ocean before manifest creation embodies this name as quiet totality before differentiation.

### 513. jīvaḥ (जीवः)
- Meaning: Life principle in all.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: When Akrura enters the Yamuna and beholds Vishnu with Ananta, he sees the transcendent form within the ordinary world; that is this name in narrative form.

### 514. vinayitāsākṣī (विनयितासाक्षी)
- Meaning: Witness of the disciplined.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a direct support for inwardness, witness-awareness, and mind-gathering contemplation.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by bringing the mind back to witnessing whenever it becomes overrun by reaction.
- Story: Kapila's instruction to Devahuti joins analysis and devotion, making this name shine as inner clarity.

### 515. mukundaḥ (मुकुन्दः)
- Meaning: Giver of liberation.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a direct pointer toward moksha as knowledge of reality rather than as a mere improved condition inside samsara.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by asking what you still take to be absolutely necessary even though it cannot survive change.
- Story: Dhruva seeks a kingdom but receives direct vision and a transformed heart; this name matches the Lord who turns ambition toward liberation.

### 516. amitavikramaḥ (अमितविक्रमः)
- Meaning: Of boundless stride and valor.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that avatara names are not metaphysical limitations of Brahman but compassionate manifestations for seekers.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by allowing the story to hold the heart steady until deeper understanding becomes possible.
- Story: The reunion with Bharata displays a form of sovereignty anchored in restraint rather than possession.

### 517. ambhonidhiḥ (अम्भोनिधिः)
- Meaning: Ocean, repository of waters.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that cosmic texture is not independent substance but appearance upheld in consciousness.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by observing change in the world while remembering the changeless that makes change knowable.
- Story: Matsya guides the ark through the deluge, showing the Lord present in waters both destructive and protective.

### 518. anantātmā (अनन्तात्मा)
- Meaning: Of infinite self.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: Dhruva's austerity ends in a vision of the Lord whose presence fills inner and outer space alike; this name belongs to that overwhelming encounter.

### 519. mahodadhiśayaḥ (महोदधिशयः)
- Meaning: He who reclines on the great ocean.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a contemplative hint that what seems manifold in nature rests in one unfragmented truth.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by allowing elemental experience to point beyond itself toward the one reality it depends on.
- Story: Krishna dances upon Kaliya in the Yamuna, purifying poisoned waters; this name aligns with divine mastery within nature.

### 520. antakaḥ (अन्तकः)
- Meaning: Ender of all at the right time.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as an aid to seeing that calendar, causation, and destiny belong to vyavahara, not to the absolute as such.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by remembering that what changes in time is not the deepest self.
- Story: Bhishma himself waits for the auspicious time of uttarayana before departing, a fitting narrative backdrop for names of divine timing and order.

### 521. ajaḥ (अजः)

- Story: Garuda carries the Lord across the worlds, yet no place contains him; the story reinforces this name's claim that Vishnu transcends location.

### 530. trivikramaḥ (त्रिविक्रमः)

### 556. puṣkarākṣaḥ (पुष्कराक्षः)
- Meaning: Lotus-eyed.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a name in which Sri becomes a contemplative symbol of harmony, grace, and all-sided completeness.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by redefining prosperity as inward clarity plus wise stewardship of what has been given.
- Story: In Tirumala lore, Srinivasa receives and protects the wealth of devotion offered by countless pilgrims; such narratives illuminate auspicious names.

### 557. mahāmanāḥ (महामनाः)
- Meaning: Great-minded.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: Dhruva's austerity ends in a vision of the Lord whose presence fills inner and outer space alike; this name belongs to that overwhelming encounter.

### 558. bhagavān (भगवान्)
- Meaning: The possessor of all divine excellences.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Garuda carries the Lord across the worlds, yet no place contains him; the story reinforces this name's claim that Vishnu transcends location.

### 559. bhagahā (भगहा)
- Meaning: Destroyer of false prosperity.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a saguna-Ishvara name through which grace, order, and dharmic correction become meditatively approachable.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by trusting order without becoming passive, and doing your dharma while leaving total control to the Lord.
- Story: When Banasura's arrogance overwhelms his own good fortune, Krishna defeats him without needless cruelty; this name shows protective justice with restraint.

### 560. ānandī (आनन्दी)
- Meaning: Joyful and joy-giving.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: At the close of each kalpa, the worlds fold back into Narayana; this name points to that cosmic re-absorption.

### 561. vanamālī (वनमाली)
- Meaning: Wearer of the forest garland.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: When mother Yashoda asked Krishna to open his mouth, she saw worlds within him; this name fits the Lord whose apparent smallness can suddenly reveal totality.

### 562. halāyudhaḥ (हलायुधः)
- Meaning: Wielder of the plough.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that avatara names are not metaphysical limitations of Brahman but compassionate manifestations for seekers.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by allowing the story to hold the heart steady until deeper understanding becomes possible.
- Story: Balarama's plough-bearing strength symbolizes grounded power that prepares and protects; names linked to Halayudha fit this steady might.

### 563. ādityaḥ (आदित्यः)
- Meaning: Son of Aditi, the radiant one.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: In the Gita's Vishvarupa revelation, Arjuna beholds all beings and all time in Krishna; this name shines where Vishnu appears as the cosmic whole.

### 564. jyotirādityaḥ (ज्योतिरादित्यः)
- Meaning: Solar splendor of light.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: During pralaya, Markandeya sees the infant Narayana on the banyan leaf holding the universe in serene play; that vision matches this boundless epithet.

### 565. sahiṣṇuḥ (सहिष्णुः)
- Meaning: Forbearing.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: From the lotus springing out of Vishnu's navel, Brahma begins creation; this name recalls the Lord as the hidden ground of all worlds.

### 566. gatisattamaḥ (गतिसत्तमः)
- Meaning: The highest goal and movement.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a contemplative invitation to move from devotional dependence to liberating recognition without discarding devotion.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by remembering that devotion need not stop at consolation; it can culminate in liberating knowledge.
- Story: Gajendra's rescue is not merely escape from a crocodile but deliverance from bondage and forgetfulness; this epithet fits that deeper release.

### 567. sudhanvā (सुधन्वा)
- Meaning: Of excellent bow.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a symbolic praise of the Lord's power to cut avidya, protect dharma, and remove inner obstruction.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by letting discrimination cut confusion before it grows into habit.
- Story: Panchajanya, Krishna's conch, announces righteous action and awakens hearts before battle; the name reflects sound as sacred power.

### 568. khaṇḍaparaśuḥ (खण्डपरशुः)
- Meaning: Wielder of the battle-axe.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Vamana's three strides cover earth, heaven, and the regions between; this name becomes visible in that act of all-pervasion.

### 569. dāruṇaḥ (दारुणः)
- Meaning: Stern and formidable to evil.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a pointer to Brahman as the substratum of all names, forms, causes, and effects.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by loosening the habit of seeing life as spiritually fragmented and remembering one presence through every perception.
- Story: Prahlada insists that Hari is present everywhere, even in a pillar; this name is affirmed by that fearless vision of omnipresence.

### 570. draviṇapradaḥ (द्रविणप्रदः)
- Meaning: Giver of wealth and resources.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: In the Bhagavata, Krishna expands himself for every gopa and calf during Brahma's bewilderment; this name suits the Lord who is one yet all.

### 571. divaḥspṛk (दिवःस्पृक्)
- Meaning: Touching the heavens.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a reminder that Vishnu is not one object in the universe, but the inner reality because of which the universe appears.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by pausing during ordinary activity and noticing that every experience shines in the same field of awareness.
- Story: Narayana resting on the cosmic ocean before manifest creation embodies this name as quiet totality before differentiation.

### 572. sarvadṛgvyāsaḥ (सर्वदृग्व्यासः)
- Meaning: The all-seeing arranger of knowledge.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a name that links devotion to viveka, because the Lord is both the revealer of truth and the ground of knowing.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by asking not only what is happening, but who is the knower in whose light the happening is known.
- Story: Sanatkumara and the sages seek the supreme truth and find it centered in Narayana; the name suits the Lord who is both teacher and taught-of.

### 573. vācaspatirayonijaḥ (वाचस्पतिरयोनिजः)
- Meaning: Lord of speech, not born from a womb.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a contemplative bridge from sacred word to direct recognition of the self-luminous reality.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by letting the name turn curiosity into discrimination and discrimination into stillness.
- Story: In the Gajendra episode, the elephant's past-life memory of prayer returns at the crucial moment; this name reflects divine knowledge awakening dormant wisdom.

### 574. trisāmā (त्रिसामा)
- Meaning: Essence of the three Sama chants.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as an aid to sarvatmakatva: the recognition that the one reality shines through the entire field of experience.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by using the name to move from scattered involvement toward the intuition of a single underlying reality.
- Story: When Akrura enters the Yamuna and beholds Vishnu with Ananta, he sees the transcendent form within the ordinary world; that is this name in narrative form.

### 575. sāmagaḥ (सामगः)

### 576. sāma (साम)
- Meaning: The Sama Veda itself, harmony.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a revelation of Vishnu as witness-consciousness and as the light by which scripture and experience become intelligible.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by joining study, self-inquiry, and devotion instead of separating them into different compartments.
- Story: Krishna instructs Arjuna on the battlefield, turning despair into discernment; this name belongs to the Lord who teaches inside crisis.

### 577. nirvāṇam (निर्वाणम्)
- Meaning: Supreme peace and release.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a direct pointer toward moksha as knowledge of reality rather than as a mere improved condition inside samsara.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by asking what you still take to be absolutely necessary even though it cannot survive change.
- Story: Ajamila's last-minute remembrance opens a path beyond the mechanics of punishment; this name points to grace beyond despair.

- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by observing change in the world while remembering the changeless that makes change knowable.
- Story: The moonlike cooling of Krishna's presence in Vraja often follows scenes of heat and turmoil; such names fit the soothing aspect of divinity in nature.

### 590. kuvaleśayaḥ (कुवलेशयः)
- Meaning: He who rests on the waters or within the lotus-world.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a reminder that sacred radiance is not opposed to truth but can refine the mind toward it.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by seeing beauty as a support for recollection rather than as a distraction to be resented.
- Story: When Sudama visits Krishna in poverty and returns to quiet abundance, the story shows auspicious grace arriving without humiliation.

### 591. gohitaḥ (गोहितः)
- Meaning: Well-wisher of cows, earth, and beings.
- Shankara lens: In a Shankara-shaped reading, this name works as a contemplative hint that what seems manifold in nature rests in one unfragmented truth.
- How to contemplate: Contemplate it by allowing elemental experience to point beyond itself toward the one reality it depends on.
- Story: In the forest episodes of the Ramayana, trees, rivers, and mountains become witnesses to Rama's dharma; this name turns the landscape into theology.

### 592. gopatiḥ (गोपतिः)
- Meaning: Lord of cows and protectees.
- Shankara lens: From the Advaita bhashya lens, this name serves as a form-centered praise that steadies devotion while quietly training the mind toward the limitless reality behind form.
- How to contemplate: Relate to it in practice by using personal devotion as the emotional purification that prepares the mind for knowledge.
- Story: Brahma's bewilderment in Vraja shows Krishna's supremacy even in apparently ordinary village life.

### 593. goptā (गोप्ता)
- Meaning: Protector.
- Shankara lens: In an Advaita mode of contemplation, this epithet becomes a support for devotion to the Lord who removes obstacles to knowledge by preserving righteousness.
- How to contemplate: Let it work on the mind by seeing the removal of confusion as one of the Lord's most important forms of protection.
- Story: In saving the elephant king, Vishnu accepts no delay because the cry is sincere; that immediacy illustrates this name.
